Module: Medical
Summary: Structured Accident & First Aid Reporting
Role: Business Manager
Source: Sheet1 - Row 19
Comment: Dear Product Team,

 I am writing to suggest an enhancement to the Arbor Accident/Injury section. While the current description-based system is a great start, transitioning to structured data fields would significantly improve reporting accuracy and pupil safety for schools.

 Proposed Enhancements

 Moving beyond a simple description box, I recommend adding specific, mandatory fields:

 Severity Rating: (e.g., Minor, Moderate, Major) for better tracking/reporting.

 Injury Location: A dropdown list of body parts for clearer medical records.

 Communication Log: A dedicated "Parent Contacted" field (Yes/No/Time).

 Treatment Administered: Standardised options to ensure consistency in care.

 Switching to structured fields allows schools to analyse data trends (such as injury hotspots) and ensures regulatory compliance is met every time a record is saved. It transforms the module from a simple log into a powerful safeguarding tool.

 I‚Äôd be happy to discuss how these specific data points and much more could be integrated to better serve your school users.

Source: Sheet1 - Row 132
Comment: Dear Arbor Support Team,

 We would like to request a feature improvement relating to the setup of school trips that take payments across academic years.

 Currently, when planning trips for the next academic year, we are required to create them with dates in August in order to enable payments. Once the new academic year begins, we then have to recreate the trip again in the correct academic year, effectively duplicating the work.

 This process significantly increases administrative workload, as trips must be set up twice, with details such as pricing, groups, deadlines, and permissions re-entered and rechecked.

 We would like to request one of the following enhancements:

 The ability to change the academic year of a trip (or its date) before payments have been taken, or

 A ‚ÄúDuplicate into next academic year‚Äù option that copies the trip structure (dates, groups, pricing, settings) without carrying over payments.

 This would allow schools to plan ahead while maintaining accurate financial reporting and would greatly reduce unnecessary admin time.

 This change would have a meaningful impact on efficiency for schools that plan trips well in advance and manage a high volume of paid activities.

 Thank you for considering this request. We would be happy to provide further detail or examples if helpful.

 Kind regards,

 Cara Pack

Ticket: PFT-9227
Issue id: 207960
Module: Behaviour
Summary: Suggestion: Improving Group Detention Creation to Reduce Teacher Workload
Role: KS4 Subject Lead Computer Science & Digital Lead of EdTech
Source: Sheet1 - Row 447
Comment: Currently, when creating a detention for a group, teachers are required to manually check that every individual student does not already have a detention scheduled on that date. This process is not feasible in practice. It creates a significant administrative burden and adds unnecessary workload for already time-pressured staff.

 At present, if even one student in a class already has a detention, the date is removed from the available list entirely. This prevents teachers from assigning detentions to the rest of the group, even when the majority of students are available. As a result, teachers must either abandon the date or manually check each student, which involves excessive clicks and time.

 Other systems (for example, Edulink) handle this more effectively by:

 -- Assigning the detention automatically to students who are available

 -- Flagging or reporting any students with clashes

 -- Informing the teacher of conflicts without blocking the entire process

 A similar approach would significantly improve usability and efficiency. Teachers do not have the capacity to follow the current multi-step checking process, and the number of clicks required is disproportionate to the task. Streamlining this workflow would reduce workload, improve staff experience, and better reflect the realities of classroom practice.

Ticket: PFT-9113
Issue id: 207487
Module: Data & Reporting
Summary: Scheduled Report Attachments breaking when the creator leaves
Role: Integrated Services Manager
Source: Sheet1 - Row 561
Comment: When an employee that created scheduled reports leaves, the attachments on the scheduled reports break. This is due to the leaving employee having their permissions revoked.

 Whilst the attachments break, the shared reports are still accessible if the recipient clicks the Arbor link and has permission to access the data included in the report.

 I understand from 2nd line support for security reasons e.g "a staff member could create a scheduled report with data and set it to email a personal address then after the staff member has left the data would still be sent to the email."

 Whilst this justification is understandable, it does create a lot of work for trusts and schools that have a single employee responsible for creating reports across the trust site as when an employee leaves each report needs to be duplicated by an active user in order for the attachments to start working. With Arbor's UX this can be a very time consuming process especially when like us there are 300+ reports that need 'repairing'.

 Perhaps a better solution for your security concerns would be allow school / trust Arbor admins to permit which domains scheduled reports can be sent to. For example, we would restrict report being sent to *@hispmat.org and *@highcliffe.school thereby preventing reports being sent to personal addresses such as *@gmail.com.

---

Role: Lead Administrator
Source: Sheet1 - Row 585

Ticket: PFT-9005
Issue id: 207001
Module: Staff/HR
Summary: Permissions overlap to be removed
Role: Data Manager
Source: Sheet1 - Row 669
Comment: There are a number of permissions where there are multiple smaller permissions lumped together. The prime example of this is the "General Admin:Administer" permission within the School category. While at face value this single permission takes on a number of high level admin tasks that should be heavily restricted, such as setting up the next school year or setting up the guardian portal. But at the same time there are a lot of very low level permissions that any normal school would look at passing off as low level admin, such as approving student profile record changes or creating meetings. With this being set up as it is, giving pastoral admin staff the low level admin tasks will also allow them to create and delete year set ups, have access to the full behavioural set up, turn on/off the guardian portal. These are a security weakness with even trying to give the lowest possible access to staff that they require will give multiple high level accesses that could be prevented with more granular permissions.

Ticket: PFT-8936
Issue id: 206787
Module: Cover
Summary: A Specialised 'Supply Teacher' Account for Registers
Role: IT Technician
Source: Sheet1 - Row 738
Comment: Years ago we had CMIS - which I hated - but it had one amazing feature, and this was that it had a supply login account for the accompanying ePortal to do the registers. The supply account was set up through some wizardry so that it had a password that automatically changed to a random string of 4 characters every night at midnight, and each morning if there was supply staff in, the office could run a report that would give them the new password. They could then hand this over to supply without worry of anyone accessing it after that day.

 Currently we have two options:

 1. Have existing staff log on for supply - this has to be someone with access to the register that is needed, so usually has to be a yeargroup partner or TA).

 2. Use a supply account that has access to all registers, but then someone has to be in charge of remembering to reset the password manually at the end of each day so nobody has access to it externally. This is cumbersome and prone to failure where said person forgets, is too busy, or is off sick.

 If we could somehow have an account coded with an automatically resetting password that would really solve the supply problem!

Ticket: PFT-8872
Issue id: 206401
Module: Communications
Summary: Club Issues
Role: Receptionist
Source: Sheet1 - Row 802
Comment: Dear Arbor Support Team,

 I am writing to formally raise several critical issues regarding the Clubs Module within the Arbor Management Information System. These technical shortcomings are currently causing significant administrative distress for our front-office staff and frustration for our parent body.

 We would like to bring the following three areas to your immediate attention:

 1. Lack of "Capacity Full" Notifications

 The system currently fails to provide a clear "Club Full" notification to parents once capacity is reached. This lack of transparency leads to a high volume of avoidable phone calls and emails from parents seeking clarification, placing an unnecessary manual burden on our administration team.

 2. Absence of Basket Expiry (Reservation Timer)

 We have identified a significant flaw in the booking workflow: parents are able to hold places in their "basket" indefinitely without completing the checkout or payment process.

 The Impact: These spaces are effectively "locked," preventing other parents from booking them, even if the initial user has no intention of following through.

 Requested Resolution: We require an automatic "release" function (a reservation timer) that returns the space to the public pool if payment is not confirmed within a set timeframe (e.g., 10‚Äì15 minutes).

 3. Ineffective Archiving on the Parent App

 The Arbor App continues to display inactive and historical clubs from previous terms and academic years. This lack of a clear "Active/Inactive" filter or automatic archiving function is causing widespread confusion. Parents are frequently attempting to view or join clubs that ended years ago because the interface is cluttered with legacy data.

 The current state of the module is not fit for purpose for a busy school environment. It is creating more work for our staff rather than streamlining it.

 Yours sincerely,

 Thorpe Hall Primary School Office
